BREAKING CHANGE\r\n\r\nThis changes the behavior of the default image `loader` so that [`Content-Disposition`](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/Headers/Content-Disposition#as_a_response_header_for_the_main_body) header is now `attachment` for added protection since the API can serve arbitrary remote images.\r\n\r\nThe new default value, `attachment`, forces the browser to download the image when visiting directly. produces to GitHub, and as such it prevents me from creating a minimal reproduction repository. The repo above is a dummy to satisfy the issue template requirements.\r\n\r\n### To Reproduce\r\n\r\nIn a WSL2 Ubuntu x64 environment (or likely other linux/unix environments):\r\n1. `yarn create next-app foobar`\r\n2. `cd foobar`\r\n3. `git remote add origin https://github.com/xxx/foobar`\r\n4. `git push origin main`\r\n\r\n### Current vs. Expected behavior\r\n\r\n### Observation\r\n\r\nIn linux/unix environments (or at the very least in WSL2 Ubuntu 20 x64, and [evidently Darwin x64](https://github.com/vercel/next.js/discussions/48956)), Yarn PnP in combination with create-next-app's templates' `.gitignore` files result in create-next-app creating project repositories with an initial commit which cannot be pushed to free GitHub repositories due to the 100M file size limitation. The large file in question appears to be the Next compiler which resides at the following location in my Next repositories:\r\n\r\n```\r\n.yarn/unplugged/@next-swc-linux-x64-gnu-npm-14.2.3-635f7187f5/node_modules/@next/swc-linux-x64-gnu/next-swc.linux-x64-gnu.node\r\n```\r\n\r\nIn my environment, the `git push` operation produces the following output:\r\n```sh\r\n$ git push origin main\r\nEnumerating objects: 798, done.\r\nCounting objects: 100% (798/798), done.\r\nDelta compression using up to 12 threads\r\nCompressing objects: 100% (782/782), done.\r\nWriting objects: 100% (798/798), 203.24 MiB | 4.00 MiB/s, done.\r\nTotal 798 (delta 13), reused 0 (delta 0), pack-reused 0\r\nremote: Resolving deltas: 100% (13/13), done.\r\nremote: error: Trace: 196be7017bc6c58f3bfa0e53058cf07f500569efac1b596ff8524f176dd0a7b7\r\nremote: error: See https://gh.io/lfs for more information.\r\nremote: error: File .yarn/unplugged/@next-swc-linux-x64-gnu-npm-14.1.0-5a9ae6f5df/node_modules/@next/swc-linux-x64-gnu/next-swc.linux-x64-gnu.node is 114.62 MB; this exceeds GitHub's file size limit of 100.00 MB\r\nremote: error: GH001: Large files detected. You may want to try Git Large File Storage - https://git-lfs.github.com.\r\nTo https://github.com/xxx/foobar.git\r\n ! [remote rejected] main -> main (pre-receive hook declined)\r\nerror: failed to push some refs to 'https://github.com/xxx/foobar.git'\r\n```\r\n\r\nResolving the issue necessitates a fair bit of research on the end-user's part, and ultimately the modification of the default `.gitignore` file provided by the templates as well as squashing or rewriting the repo's history to exclude the problematic files. Alternately - if users instead follow the advice suggested by the `git` error - they may end up down a different rabbit hole, setting up Git LFS (and likely engaging GitHub's LFS services which may incur costs in short order) just to handle the SWC binary.\r\n\r\nThe issue is [compounded in downstream tools such as Cloudflare's `create-cloudflare`](https://github.com/cloudflare/workers-sdk/issues/5790), which themselves may create additional commits on top of the one which create-next-app makes, further cementing the problematic file's inclusion in the fresh project repository's history.\r\n\r\n### Expectation\r\n\r\nProject repositories created via create-next-app should be able to be pushed to a free GitHub repository immediately, without requiring the end-user to modify default files and squashing/rewriting repository history or set up Git LFS.\r\n\r\n### Provide environment information\r\n\r\n```bash\r\nOperating System:\r\n  Platform: linux\r\n  Arch: x64\r\n  Version: #1 SMP Wed Mar 2 00:30:59 UTC 2022\r\nBinaries:\r\n  Node: 20.11.1\r\n  npm: 10.2.4\r\n  Yarn: 4.2.2\r\n  pnpm: N/A\r\nRelevant Packages:\r\n  next: 14.1.0\r\n  eslint-config-next: 14.1.0\r\n  react: 18.3.1\r\n  react-dom: 18.3.1\r\n  typescript: 5.4.5\r\nNext.js Config:\r\n  output: N/A\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n### Which area(s) are affected? What\r\n\r\nRemove the extra `__esModule` and `$$typeof` export for ESM client module\r\n\r\nFor a client page reference, it changed on server side in renderer:\r\n\r\nPrevious: `{ __esModule, $$typeof, default }`\r\nNow: `{ default }`\r\n\r\n### Why\r\n\r\nThe Module object itself appears as a client reference but it can't be rendered since it's not a real reference. I'm not sure why it was added but I think the right thing for an ESM module is to not treat the module itself as a client reference but only the objects inside of it. E.g. the \"default\" export. That's what React does upstream for ESM modules.\r\n\r\nCloses What\r\n\r\nRemove the auto appending `.xml` extension to the sitemap routes when it's a dynamic route.\r\n\r\n\r\n### Why\r\n\r\nPreviously we were adding `.xml` to `/[...paths/]sitemap` routes, but the bad part is when you use it to generate multiple sitemaps with `generateSitemaps` in format like `/[...paths/]sitemap.xml/[id]`, which doesn't look good in url format and it can be inferred as xml with content-type. Hence we don't need to add `.xml` in the url.\r\n\r\nBefore this change it could also result into the different url between dev and prod:\r\ndev: `/sitemap.xml/[id]`\r\nprod: `/sitemap/[id].xml` \r\n\r\nNow it's going to be aligned as `/sitemap/[id]`. Users can add extension flexiblely.\r\n\r\nCloses NEXT-3357","reactions":{"url":"https://api.github.com/repos/vercel/next.js/issues/65507/reactions","total_count":0,"+1":0,"-1":0,"laugh":0,"hooray":0,"confused":0,"heart":0,"rocket":0,"eyes":0},"timeline_url":"https://api.github.com/repos/vercel/next.js/issues/65507/timeline","performed_via_github_app":null,"state_reason":null}]
